## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / dynamical concentration models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A(t), which is the standard object modeled in chemical kinetics via ordinary differential equations (rate laws). With only t and A available, plausible structures are elementary/empirical rate laws, time-varying rate coefficients, reversible/parallel consumption terms, and inhibition/autocatalysis expressed directly as dA_dt = f(t, A).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate source/sink, e.g., zeroth-order kinetics or constant feed)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (elementary unimolecular consumption; exponential decay in A)
- Second-order decay (self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular A+A consumption; faster-than-exponential decay)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order c1)
- Affine in concentration (source + first-order loss): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant production with linear removal; approach to steady state)
- Parallel pathways / mixed orders: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular loss channels)
- Reversible approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (interpretable as net forward-backward with A driven toward c0/c1 when other species are buffered)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplifying production with depletion/limit; sigmoidal A(t) possible)
- Inhibition / crowding rational form: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at large A due to inhibition/limited active sites)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (aging catalyst, temperature ramp, or changing conditions over time)
- Time-varying source term (pulse/decay drive): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) - c2 * A (externally driven feed or activation that changes exponentially in time)
- Diffusion-/transport-limited decay surrogate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (t + c1) (effective slowing of kinetics over time due to transport limitations or depletion boundary layers)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Ôćĺ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Ôćĺ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Ôćĺ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Ôćĺ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Ôćĺ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption vs production sign: predominantly negative dA_dt indicates net depletion of A; positive indicates net generation or feed.
- Reaction order identification: if dA_dt scales roughly linearly with A Ôćĺ first-order; curvature consistent with A**2 or A**n suggests higher order or autocatalysis.
- Steady-state approach: structures like dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A imply convergence to A* = c0 / c1 (homeostatic/buffered behavior).
- Multiple pathways: sums of terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) indicate parallel mechanisms with different dependence on A dominating in different regimes.
- Time-dependent coefficients: explicit t multiplying A (or appearing in denominators) suggests changing environment/catalyst activity rather than intrinsic constant kinetics.
- Inhibition/limited-capacity effects: rational forms in A (e.g., A/(A+c1)) imply diminishing marginal rate increase at high A (site limitation, self-inhibition).
- Autocatalysis signature: factors like A*(c1-A) or A*(c0+c1*A) imply self-acceleration at low A and saturation/slowdown near a carrying level.
- Transport-limited regimes: decay rates that weaken with time (e.g., division by (t+c1)) can mimic diffusion boundary-layer growth or mixing limitations.
